This is a fairly old and ongoing effort on the part of Chinese. I am not very sure that it is supported by some official agency, but seeing the amount of effort involved and the resources available, it is hard not to believe so. During my association with the Govt the impression that I got was that while we were very much aware of these activities and the steps required to protect ourselves, but the inherent inertia in govt organisations prevented any proactive approach. 

Of the agencies chartered to protect our critical information infrastructure, the less said the better. One of these issued an advisory against Lenovo laptops bringing out a malicious executable of which the examiner knew nothing about. Google research proved the "offending" file to be a sound card driver !!! 

Subhash Dutta

From purohitsingh2 at gmail.com  Fri Apr  9 06:04:25 2010

Dear All,

Could anyone provide the differences between Content Spoofing and HTML
Injection ?  Is it just a naming convention (WASC verses OWASP) ?

regards,
purohit

From nath at computer.org  Sun Apr 11 10:41:38 2010
From: nath at computer.org (CPC)
Date: Sun, 11 Apr 2010 07:41:38 -0700
Subject: [Owasp-delhi] Content Spoofing / HTML Injection
In-Reply-To: <z2jd7b6f19b1004090304y202d0db3ze31e2a52ea952cf9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <z2jd7b6f19b1004090304y202d0db3ze31e2a52ea952cf9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <q2qc0ec57ae1004110741g1cf565c2i7cc4081ca0422d5f@mail.gmail.com>

Content spoofing is used in phishing scams as a method of forcing a
legitimate website to deliver or redirect users to bogus content. For
example, users often receive a suspicious link that instructs them to
confirm their user name and password information. Typically, phishing
websites are hosted on look-alike domain names mimicking the content of the
real site. In the case of Content spoofing phishing scams, fake content is
injected into the real website, making it very difficult, if not impossible,
for users to detect the difference and therefore protect themselves.


HTML Injection refers to injecting HTML code into a web servers response to
alter the content to the end user.

HTML injection may cause many type of vulnerabilities content spoofing and
even XSS.

One is the cause, and the other a result of the cause.

Does that make sense?

Chandra

Logical errors are, I think, of greater practical importance than many

opinion on every subject in turn. Source: Bertrand Russell, A History of

hi;

In content spoofing there is not only html based injection but it can be
done various ways like  e-mail (phishing), bulletin-board postings(XSS) and
chat-room transmissions(XSS). An attacker may modify information and links
in an  Web site by accessing and altering content on the server if there is
lack of permission.

From sripathi.krishnan at gmail.com  Sun Apr 11 15:11:41 2010
From: sripathi.krishnan at gmail.com (Sripathi Krishnan)
Date: Mon, 12 Apr 2010 00:41:41 +0530
Subject: [Owasp-delhi] Content Spoofing / HTML Injection
In-Reply-To: <z2jd7b6f19b1004090304y202d0db3ze31e2a52ea952cf9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <z2jd7b6f19b1004090304y202d0db3ze31e2a52ea952cf9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <q2z7a4a5faf1004111211kfe67cda4w9211152e05c65fc7@mail.gmail.com>

**From mitre.org - http://capec.mitre.org/data/definitions/148.html

> [*In Content Spoofing*] an attacker modifies content to make it contain
> something other than what the original content producer intended while
> keeping the apparent source of the content unchanged [...] Content can be
> modified at the source (e.g. modifying the source file for a web page) or in
> transit (e.g. intercepting and modifying a message between the sender and
> recipient).
>

Content Spoofing is a general concept. If I am the administrator of a
company's proxy server, I can modify the content before it reaches the
employees. This would be called content spoofing. Spam emails claiming to
come from a bank are also a type of content spoofing.

HTML Injection is just one of the several ways to spoof content. It is
similar in concept to XSS, except that here you are trying to inject HTML
instead of Javascript. Its by far the easiest way to spoof content, and very
much prevalent.

--Sri

http://blog.530geeks.com

From: nileshkumar83 at gmail.com (nileshkumar83 at gmail.com)

Subject: [Owasp-delhi] Content Spoofing / HTML Injection
In-Reply-To: <z2jd7b6f19b1004090304y202d0db3ze31e2a52ea952cf9@mail.gmail.com>

As per my knowledge there's not much difference. HTML Injection is the way
to do Content Spoofing. In other words HTML Injection is a vulnerability and
Content Spoofing is a consequence of that (attack). Altering the contents of
a page by injecting fake contents may actually change the content of the
article.

Hi List, 

Let me direct your attention to a phishing email sent on behalf of PNB. The link to update personal banking details has not been as yet flagged as a phishing site by Firefox. The site is based in Tehran and is hosted by Iran Islamic Republic of Information Technology Company. After filling in the details, the site redirects to the actual PNB site. 

The initial email has been sent from a server in Luxembourg (217.31.76.121) and routed through China located at 203.156.254.26. 

The best part is the page where the log-in details and transaction passed are asked for has warning messages to beware of phishing !!!

I would always recommend SSL, to make sure my passwords are not on plain
text. It also depends on your companies policies on how you treat them.

not mandatory within the organization. However, as a security person, I
would want to protect my data all round.

This is all about mitigating the risk..  (If there is no control in
place, there is risk. If all the relevant controls are in place, still
there would be some risk).
 
That's depends upon the business, how they would like to proceed with RA
(Risk Assessment). If they find the application is critical to business
they will put extra control in place like having SSL, if the application
has least severity in terms of impacting the business.. they may not go
with the SSL.
 
I hope this will clarify your doubts.

From imanilsaini at gmail.com  Tue Apr 27 22:57:40 2010
From: imanilsaini at gmail.com (anil saini)
Date: Wed, 28 Apr 2010 07:57:40 +0500
Subject: [Owasp-delhi] Owasp-delhi Digest, Vol 33, Issue 6
In-Reply-To: <mailman.2444.1272375266.2290.owasp-delhi@lists.owasp.org>
References: <mailman.2444.1272375266.2290.owasp-delhi@lists.owasp.org>
Message-ID: <j2i4dc9ad931004271957j5f1ceee6n2f0a4fe825e6ebdb@mail.gmail.com>

It is a very good question and i have seen organisations do not have a clear
cut idea weather they should implement SSL inside organisation or not.
            The answer for this question comes straight from Risk Assessment
& Risk Management. If You have an important application into your
organisation which is authenticated by passwords then you have the risk of
sniffing passwords. Now, how do you manage this risk?  By applying some kind
of control. And implementing SSL is one of the control .
            So weather to implement SSL or create VLAN for segregation of
traffic depends on Risk Assessment and Risk Management.

From sripathi.krishnan at gmail.com  Wed Apr 28 01:29:30 2010
From: sripathi.krishnan at gmail.com (Sripathi Krishnan)
Date: Wed, 28 Apr 2010 10:59:30 +0530
Subject: [Owasp-delhi] SQL Injection+XSS < Input Sanitization
In-Reply-To: <20100427163800.28736.qmail@f5mail-236-240.rediffmail.com>
References: <20100427163800.28736.qmail@f5mail-236-240.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <g2o7a4a5faf1004272229z15264d7cq619d4341ef94be2e@mail.gmail.com>

>
> Can input sanitization mitigate sql injection ? If yes how and if no why ?
>

No.
Suppose you have a "first name" input field, and the user enters the text
d'souza. Its a valid name, so input sanitization will pass. But if you take
the name and directly create a query, you will get a SQL injection because
of the extra single quote.

In general, you may have inputs that are valid for your domain, but if you
directly use them to create a query - they will cause injection. I

To prevent SQL Injection, use parameterized queries (eg. PreparedStatement).
Avoid dynamically created queries; but if you must, make sure you escape
users input. The reference ESAPI library provides escape methods for popular
databases.

For resolving xss, why output sanitization is considered ? Why not input
> sanitization ?
>
Because you don't know whether the data is going to end up in HTML or
Javascript or CSS or in a PDF file. Each output format has a different
escape function.

Consider the subject of your email "SQL Injection+XSS < Input Sanitization".
It contains the special characters <.
Now, you can approach this problem in several ways. I'll try to explain the
problem with each of them.

   1. Don't allow special characters - this is too restrictive, and not
   always possible.
   2. Encode < as &lt; and store in database - Problem is that &lt; only
   works in HTML. If you want to use the same string in Javascript or in your
   javacode, you will have a problem (the text will be shown as &lt;). In
   general, you don't know where you are going to use the data, so you can't
   encode it at input time.

The solution is to always escape the data just before you rendering the
output. If you are creating HTML, escape according to HTML rules. If its
javascript, escape according to javascript rules. This page explains how
output encoding works <http://www.530geeks.com/encode.jsp>.

--Sri

Dude, mind your language. I may be a smartass, and I may be blatantly wrong.
But this is a public forum, and you don't have the right to use such
language.

Firstly, obfuscated JS is a strict no-no.
>
You could paste the obfuscated JS code into the email, right? Did your email
client tell you 'sorry, you can't send js code in an email?'. The job of the
email client / facebook page is to treat the js code as data, escape it
properly and ensure that it doesn't automatically execute when you open the
email or view the page. I believe facebook is doing that - the js code
doesn't automatically execute.

Secondly, it automatically prompts and executes the "Invite your Friends to
> this page" (something like that) widget. Tell me how can you do that?
>
Sure - but only after the user has copied the javascript code, pasted it in
the address bar and hit enter. I can send the same js code in an email to my
friends and tell them to copy/paste into address bar. It will work, and it
has nothing to do with facebook.

In theory, you could come up with javascript code to automatically send an
email from your gmail account. The point is - gmail will never auto-execute
the code. But if the user is stupid to copy/paste it into his address bar,
nothing can help him.


--Sri
http://blog.530geeks.com

Message-ID: <o2l36db492b1004281142l13297b49wefb02e7f896452cb@mail.gmail.com>

It all depends on why you were considering the deployment earlier ? Also, I
am interested in knowing what do you need it for ?

SSL is a layer of security which lies between transport layer and
application layer. It is very useful for preventing man-in-the-middle
attacks in an organization i.e. the insider attacks. Deploying this on your
file server (sftp) would definitely slow down the file transfer process but
would ensure the secure transfer. SSL provides you resilience from attacks,
IDS provides you the property of detection & recovery. You would also look
at other security properties like Prevention and Deterrence.

Thanks,

Nipun

> will put extra control in place like having SSL, if the application has
> least severity in terms of impacting the business.. they may not go with the
> SSL.*
> **

thank you all for your comments. Perhaps if I ran a poll, I reckon 97% of
you would agree SSL should be considered within the organisation as well.

from a holistic risk approach, and security best practice, perhaps SSL is
necessary. But this is within the perimeter, and within your stronghold..

But tell me fellas, how many of you have come across an organisation which
has suffered due to the lack of it..
